        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428073369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8481322758574363112">With many thanks to my friend, Will Byrnes, I read The Round House and while stingy with five stars, this book was without question, five stars. If I could give it more, I would.<br/><br/>I had prior knowledge of the problem of crimes against women on U. S. Indian Reservations specifically the inability of determining jurisdiction of areas, adding to the fact (due to a U.S. Supreme Court ruling) that on the reservation, non-Indians cannot be charged with crimes committed on Indian reservations, so I wasn’</span>
  <span id="freeText8481322758574363112" style="display:none">With many thanks to my friend, Will Byrnes, I read The Round House and while stingy with five stars, this book was without question, five stars. If I could give it more, I would.<br /><br />I had prior knowledge of the problem of crimes against women on U. S. Indian Reservations specifically the inability of determining jurisdiction of areas, adding to the fact (due to a U.S. Supreme Court ruling) that on the reservation, non-Indians cannot be charged with crimes committed on Indian reservations, so I wasn’t surprised with the storyline, actually two intertwining storylines, both of which were exceptional. <br /> <br />Some facts on crimes against women on U. S. Indian reservations:<br />•	Native women suffer violent crime at the highest rates in the country.<br />•	On many reservations, Native women are murdered at a rate more than 10 times the national average.<br />•	Violent crime rates in Indian Country are more than 2.5 times the national rate; some reservations face a rate 20 times higher.*<br /><br /><b>August 23, 2012</b><br />“Early this week, two U.S. House Representatives members and the Tacoma News Tribune took clear stands against protecting women from sexual assault. Representatives Todd Akin, R-Missouri, and Steve King, R-Iowa, did so by promoting the concept of “legitimate rape.” The News Tribune did so by attacking the only real hope for combating the national pandemic of violence against Native women.” (Later in the story, then VP candidate Paul Ryan voted to omit the tribal protections.)* <br />*<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://crosscut.com/2012/08/23/gender/110172/revictimizing-native-women-political-purposes/">http://crosscut.com/2012/08/23/gender...</a><br /><br /><b>As a nation, what is wrong with us, this continued injustice?</b> <br /><br /><b>My brief review</b> <br />Louise Erdrich successfully blended dialog, scenery and storylines into two related and life changing events; the rape of a wife and mother and the ‘coming of age’ for her son, Joe. The Ojibwe reservation is where the mother, Geraldine helps women on the reservation, the father, Bazil, a tribal judge and the story as told by their 13 year old, Joe.<br /><br />Geraldine, the woman, is brutally raped and afterward without telling anything about the assault, goes into self-imposed seclusion leaving Joe and his father, rudderless. <br /> <br />Joe and his two devoted friends support him in his efforts to try to determine who was responsible for changing his life so quickly and dramatically. They want to make it right again.<br /> <br />For an in depth and superb review, my friend Will Byrnes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370459770" rel="nofollow noopener">The Round House</a> offers the best. After reading Will’s review you will surely call or go to your library or bookstore get the book, put down what you’re reading and begin an unforgettable journey delivered by Louise Erdrich and enhanced only by Will's review. <br /><br />Further links to the subject of crimes against women on U. S. Indian reservations:<br /> <br />From Indian Law Resource Center<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.indianlaw.org/safewomen/violence-against-native-women-gaining-global-attention">http://www.indianlaw.org/safewomen/vi...</a><br /><br />Futures without Violence - <a href="http://www.futureswithoutviolence.org/userfiles/file/Violence%20Against%20AI%20AN%20Women%20Fact%20Sheet.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">Violence Against Women</a> **<br /><br />** “The confusing division of authority among tribal, federal and state governments results in a jurisdictional maze that is complicated by the lack of tribal courts’ criminal jurisdiction over non-Indians, the practical impact of Public Law 280, and other limitations on tribal criminal jurisdiction.”<br /><br />While Aljazeer is certainly a controversial news organization, curiously enough this was the very most comprehensive fact, figures and videos about violence against women on United States Indian Reservations.<br /><a href="http://stream.aljazeera.com/story/justice-denied-native-american-women-0022344" rel="nofollow noopener">Justice Denied</a> <br /> <br />#####<br /><br />NT Times <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/05/23/us/native-americans-struggle-with-high-rate-of-rape.html?pagewanted=all&lt;br%20/&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener">Native Americans Struggle With Reservation Rape</a> article, May 22 , 2012<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8481322758574363112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2927044535679095412">This is one of those stories I can't imagine 'ever' forgetting. <br/>WOW-WOW-WOW...."The WRITING" by Louise Erdrich was EXCEPTIONAL. I wish *I* had words to describe what she 'did' on paper what I liked SOOOOOOOOO much. (I loved how the author 'inserted' ADULT *Joe* like a 'drop-of-spilled-water' into the story---then carried on 'BEING' young *Joe*: smooth -as- silk!)<br/>Readers ALMOST didn't notice what SHE was doing. I loved how the author gave us 'enough' information needed --but not 'too much'. <br/><br/>DAMN:</span>
  <span id="freeText2927044535679095412" style="display:none">This is one of those stories I can't imagine 'ever' forgetting. <br />WOW-WOW-WOW...."The WRITING" by Louise Erdrich was EXCEPTIONAL. I wish *I* had words to describe what she 'did' on paper what I liked SOOOOOOOOO much. (I loved how the author 'inserted' ADULT *Joe* like a 'drop-of-spilled-water' into the story---then carried on 'BEING' young *Joe*: smooth -as- silk!)<br />Readers ALMOST didn't notice what SHE was doing. I loved how the author gave us 'enough' information needed --but not 'too much'. <br /><br />DAMN: I'm sorry: I wish I knew how to write a better review-- wish I could 'communicate' all the feelings inside me --my thoughts -etc.<br />--I can't seem to find to words to say what it is I'm trying to say....but THIS author did **SOMETHING** very subtle with her writing-style which was BRILLIANT. <br />The writing was GORGEOUS!!!!!<br />I HAD to SLOW down and SAVOR sentences!!!!! I have 8 full pages of notes!!! <br /><br />I had TONS of enjoyment LEARNING new words<br />Learning about plants I've never heard of in my entire life --<br />I enjoyed the BIG Birthday Bash<br />The Pow-Wow Party<br />I LOVED Joe &amp; Cappy!!!<br />I loved Moonshum --Sonja-Whitey-Father Travis - Linda Lark -even the 'sub' characters like 'pimply-guy'. <br />I enjoyed 'The bonding-of-the boys'<br />I enjoyed the story-the mystery -THE TRIBE-the history-my education ----(a range of many feelings) <br />I cried on page 246 (shhhhhhhh: about Joe's father's neckties) --Don't even ask me to explain why....lol<br />I cried again when the book ended -- (I was INVESTED in this book --with pen &amp; paper)<br />I cried one more time when I read 'about-the-author' and other 'real-facts'. <br /><br />I COMPLETELY enjoyed reading ALL the MANY different reviews Goodread members wrote --(from low stars to high rating stars). I had not read these until today (after I had read the book). Making the experience MUCH more rich. I enjoyed all the postive AND negative comments. <br /><br />I'm THRILLED "The Round House" is our local BOOK CLUB 'pick' this month. I can't wait to participate with our Bay Area book club members to discuss this book. ---Sat. morning: Dec. 21st. I know our discussion will ADD to the flavor of reading this story.<br /><br />I felt 'loss' when this book ended ---(I just didn't want it to end) --- I wanted to hang out longer with Joe, Cappy, Moonshum --and the 'gang'....<br /><br /><br />Many wonderful things to say about this book!!....<br /><br />I must go....[make some bannock]....ha ha ha<br />And, Find the lost children:<br /><br /> "Papoose on the loose"!!!! <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2505889634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2505889634" />
    <a title="Meike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59050228-meike"><img alt="Meike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514995700p2/59050228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2505889634?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meike" href="/user/show/59050228-meike">Meike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2505889634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4436715321827111787">Native American author Louise Erdrich successfully blends crime fiction with a revenge tale, a coming-of-age story, a narrative about racism and the depiction of life on a reservation - this is the stuff that National Book Award winners are made of. At the heart of "The Round House" lies a specific social justice issue: While Native American tribes have their own courts, they can only prosecute tribal members - but over 80% of the perpetrators of rapes on reservations are non-Native, and most ar</span>
  <span id="freeText4436715321827111787" style="display:none">Native American author Louise Erdrich successfully blends crime fiction with a revenge tale, a coming-of-age story, a narrative about racism and the depiction of life on a reservation - this is the stuff that National Book Award winners are made of. At the heart of "The Round House" lies a specific social justice issue: While Native American tribes have their own courts, they can only prosecute tribal members - but over 80% of the perpetrators of rapes on reservations are non-Native, and most are not prosecuted. Erdrich shines a light on that injustice, which is of course terrible for Native women, but should concern every American interested in protecting <i>all</i> cititzens under the rule of law. <br /><br />Our protagonist is 13-year-old Joe, who is the son of a tribal judge on a reservation in North Dakota. When his mother, a specialist for tribal enrollment, is abducted and brutally raped near the ceremonial round house, it is impossible to determine whether the crime happened on state or tribal land, so even when the perpetrator is finally found, he is not prosecuted. The repercussions will change Joe's life forever...<br /><br />The biggest strength of the book is the character of Joe - Erdrich does a fantastic job when she describes how he starts to grasp what the events around him mean for him, and what they say about society as a whole. Joe's friendship with Cappy and the relationship with this family, including his aunt and his grandfather, are also masterfully drawn. On top of that, the book does its job as a crime novel: It's full of suspense, and when the rapist is identified, the story gets even more intense. <br /><br />So hey, Booker judges: Next time you are looking for something that transcends the genre of the crime novel, this should be the benchmark. In comparison, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35687802.Snap" title="Snap by Belinda Bauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Snap</a> looks like a joke.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4436715321827111787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_434672092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mij Woodward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5222282-mij-woodward"><img alt="Mij Woodward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301943748p2/5222282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434672092?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mij Woodward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mij Woodward" href="/user/show/5222282-mij-woodward">Mij Woodward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5222282-mij-woodward?shelf=national-book-2012">national-book-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5222282-mij-woodward?shelf=hist-fiction">hist-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434672092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10588269681891419760">Maybe it's my age (68). Maybe it's a peculiar idiosyncrasy that I am unable to tolerate ANY passages in a novel that seem to be aimed at teaching me something.<br/><br/>I do like to be taught. But in a novel, any teachings have to be cleverly disguised, and just sort of snuck into the plot. <br/><br/>Maybe all that I learned about the Chippewa in North Dakota, and the injustices they and other Native groups face from our country's stupid fractured legal system, and life on the reservation--maybe that learning deser</span>
  <span id="freeText10588269681891419760" style="display:none">Maybe it's my age (68). Maybe it's a peculiar idiosyncrasy that I am unable to tolerate ANY passages in a novel that seem to be aimed at teaching me something.<br /><br />I do like to be taught. But in a novel, any teachings have to be cleverly disguised, and just sort of snuck into the plot. <br /><br />Maybe all that I learned about the Chippewa in North Dakota, and the injustices they and other Native groups face from our country's stupid fractured legal system, and life on the reservation--maybe that learning deserves 4 or 5 stars.<br /><br />However, I can only give this 3 stars, because of the passages in this novel that felt like I was being taught something.<br /><br />I only wanted to stay with the storyline, the main plot, and the main characters.<br /><br />About half way through, I began to sort of skim through the teaching passages, and other passages that did not seem germane to the storyline.<br /><br />Also, as the mother of four boys, (POSSIBLE SPOILER HERE)--I could not picture my 13-year-old boys acting in the ways that a couple of them did in this novel. Did not seem plausible. But then, our family did not have to face what the family in The Round House had to face, and also, we did not live on a reservation. <br /><br />On the plus side--I very much enjoyed the story, and will not be forgetting it and some of the characters any time soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10588269681891419760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1923503213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923503213" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923503213?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/16178586-the-round-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=community">community</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=crime-novel">crime-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=literary-novel">literary-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-novel">american-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923503213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5869090517480118985">Spring 1988. A woman is attacked and brutally raped somewhere in the Indian reservation. Joe, the thirteen-year-old son of Geraldine Coutts experienced the shock, horror and drama of his mother's condition when he and his father, Bazil, the tribal judge rushed her off to hospital. <br/><br/>Geraldine's only way of recovering was to shut herself up in a shell of silence and darkness, while the young boy struggled to grow up before the sun rose the next morning. Together with his father, and his best friend</span>
  <span id="freeText5869090517480118985" style="display:none">Spring 1988. A woman is attacked and brutally raped somewhere in the Indian reservation. Joe, the thirteen-year-old son of Geraldine Coutts experienced the shock, horror and drama of his mother's condition when he and his father, Bazil, the tribal judge rushed her off to hospital. <br /><br />Geraldine's only way of recovering was to shut herself up in a shell of silence and darkness, while the young boy struggled to grow up before the sun rose the next morning. Together with his father, and his best friends, Cappy, Zack and Angus, he tried to find answers for adult challenges he is not grown-up enough yet to handle. His transformation from young boy to adult was suddenly inevitable and the consequences unforeseen.<br /><br />COMMENTS<br />I've been holding out on this book for far too long. It was one of those experiences which will stay with me for a long time. The writing was terrific. The suspense in the book was way too drawn out since so many cultural and traditional aspects of the Indian reservation near Bismarck in North Dakota was worked into the plot. However, the characters, stories and myths added such a richness to the tale, that the book would have been a lot poorer without it. The setting was beautiful, and sharing Jo's journey through his discovery of life, unforgettable. <br /><br />I don't want to say too much about this book. It is not a YA read. Not at all. It is just one of those reads that left me sad when I finally closed it. I felt so embedded in the story. So part of the community who formed a circle around the effected and traumatized family.<br /><br />I love this author's work. This is my first encounter with Louise Erdrich and I would really like to follow it up with some of her other books. <br /><br />RECOMMENDED</span>
  <a data-text-id="5869090517480118985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37767425-the-round-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=2018-top-25">2018-top-25</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=north-america">north-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=social-commentary">social-commentary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=law">law</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=native-american">native-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=family-dynamics">family-dynamics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090797994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6773630052814571210">Set in 1988 on an Ojibwe reservation in North Dakota, thirteen-year-old Joe’s family is devastated when his mother is subject to a vicious attack. Her reaction is to withdraw, showing all the symptoms of post-traumatic stress disorder. Unfortunately, the exact location of the crime is unclear, leading to a quandary among state, federal, and tribal jurisdictions. Joe’s father is a tribal judge, so he helps Joe understand legal ramifications. It starts out as a mystery, with Joe and his friends at</span>
  <span id="freeText6773630052814571210" style="display:none">Set in 1988 on an Ojibwe reservation in North Dakota, thirteen-year-old Joe’s family is devastated when his mother is subject to a vicious attack. Her reaction is to withdraw, showing all the symptoms of post-traumatic stress disorder. Unfortunately, the exact location of the crime is unclear, leading to a quandary among state, federal, and tribal jurisdictions. Joe’s father is a tribal judge, so he helps Joe understand legal ramifications. It starts out as a mystery, with Joe and his friends attempting to figure out the perpetrator through a variety of means, but it is not what I’d call a typical mystery, as we rather quickly learn who committed the crime, and it turns into a question of whether justice will be served. Themes include the impact of violent crime on families, the desire for justice in the face of legal loopholes, personal integrity, and retribution. It is a social commentary, but the author delivers her message through the story and it is not at all heavy-handed. <br /><br />This book has it all when it comes to delivery. It contains an intriguing plot and well-developed, interesting characters. It is engrossing, well-written, and unique. It has a strong sense of place and comes across as authentic. Heads up for violence (including murder and rape), sexual content, profanity, and underage drinking. Highly recommended to readers of literary fiction, especially involving family dynamics, or those interested in Native American issues. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6773630052814571210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_580355580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/580355580" />
    <a title="Darlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1809697-darlene"><img alt="Darlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581117415p2/1809697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/580355580?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darlene" href="/user/show/1809697-darlene">Darlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580355580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1818500035309125077">It was a Sunday morning in the spring of 1988 that Geraldine Coutts, a member of the Ojibwe tribe of North Dakota, whose job and responsibility it was to determine eligibility for tribal membership, hurriedly and appearing distraught, left her home for an unexpected meeting. When she returned home later that day to her husband Bazil and son Joe, they were shocked by her condition... covered with blood and appearing to be in shock. Geraldine Coutts had been severely beaten and brutally raped and </span>
  <span id="freeText1818500035309125077" style="display:none">It was a Sunday morning in the spring of 1988 that Geraldine Coutts, a member of the Ojibwe tribe of North Dakota, whose job and responsibility it was to determine eligibility for tribal membership, hurriedly and appearing distraught, left her home for an unexpected meeting. When she returned home later that day to her husband Bazil and son Joe, they were shocked by her condition... covered with blood and appearing to be in shock. Geraldine Coutts had been severely beaten and brutally raped and the perpetrator had doused her with gasoline and attempted to set her afire. This sets the scene for Louise Erdrich's magnificent book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13602426.The_Round_House" title="The Round House by Louise Erdrich" rel="nofollow noopener">The Round House</a>.<br /><br />As in so many of Ms. Erdrich's books, there are so many layers to the story she so beautifully tells. At its most basic level, this is the story of the brutal rape of a woman and the damage this rape causes to the woman and her family... not just the physical wounds but also the psychological, emotional and even spiritual wounds. Ms. Erdrich describes the aftermath of this brutal rape with such sensitivity and yet she still manages to portray the very real devastation to Geraldine, Bazil and Joe. <br /><br />Another layer to this story which I found interesting was the legal and political aspects of life on a reservation. I found it amazing that even though the story is set in 1988, the legal problems encountered on tribal lands , as those which were experienced by Geraldine and her family who just wanted justice to be served, were and are the same experienced on tribal lands today. In recent years in fact, the Congress of the United States was arguing about and holding up the passage of the Violence Against Women Act because of a provision pertaining to crimes committed on tribal lands by non-Native American perpetrators. Ms. Erdrich does a great job of portraying the problems faced by Native Americans on tribal lands. exactly where the crime was committed and whether the perpetrator was a member of the tribe was pertinent to whether justice would be served... was the crime committed on the reservation? If not, the perpetrator would be governed by the laws of the state or even federal governments. Also, tribal laws had no 'teeth' with regards to crimes committed against Native Americans by non-Native Americans. As Bazil attempted to explain to Joe... " We want the right to prosecute criminals of all races on all lands within our original borders." This aspect of the story was extremely frustrating for me to read... I felt the frustration of Bazil (a tribal judge) and I felt Geraldine's despair and fear that she might never get her life back.<br /><br />As in other novels by Ms. Erdrich, another layer to this story which I particularly enjoyed is the tribal mysticism which was woven into the storyline... the customs and stories which are handed down from one generation to the next. In this story, Ms. Erdrich also ties in the beliefs of Catholicism .. the many types of sin and the various definitions of evil in this world. These descriptions provided a backdrop and deeper understanding of these characters ... how they felt and what motivated their actions. <br /><br />Ms. Erdrich has once again written a book that I could not put down. This story elicited my outrage over the denial of justice to Native Americans throughout American history. It elicited feelings of compassion and admiration for Geraldine and her family. Ms. Erdrich has written a story grounded in the harsh realities of Native American life on reservations and combined that harshness with the beautiful mysticism of their culture and their beliefs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1818500035309125077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_480289162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480289162" />
    <a title="Diane Yannick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1253673-diane-yannick"><img alt="Diane Yannick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468376907p2/1253673.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/480289162?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane Yannick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane Yannick" href="/user/show/1253673-diane-yannick">Diane Yannick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer480289162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13012062105954104432">National Book Award? Not for me. An important Native American legal loophole was brought to light.---when a Native American woman is raped by a non-native man, legal jurisprudence is lacking. For me, this could have been done more effectively with a tighter, more focused story.<br/><br/>I cared about Joe, the 13 year old whose mother was raped. I appreciated the author's authentic voice and her use of elder's stories when they directly related to the storyline.<br/><br/>What I didn't like was all of those rambling </span>
  <span id="freeText13012062105954104432" style="display:none">National Book Award? Not for me. An important Native American legal loophole was brought to light.---when a Native American woman is raped by a non-native man, legal jurisprudence is lacking. For me, this could have been done more effectively with a tighter, more focused story.<br /><br />I cared about Joe, the 13 year old whose mother was raped. I appreciated the author's authentic voice and her use of elder's stories when they directly related to the storyline.<br /><br />What I didn't like was all of those rambling side stories---Mooshum, to name one, and many of the tangents with Joe and his other coming of age buddies. I found some of the descriptive prose over the top and I have a high threshold for description. I know that the elimination of quotation marks is getting more and more prevalent. In this story, it was sometimes hard to separate interior monologue from dialogue. <br /><br />I have decided that I'm not a big Louise Erdrich fan. I've read 3 of her books and haven't loved any of them. Think I'm moving on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13012062105954104432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_657693896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/657693896" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/657693896?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780062273857" href="/book/show/18038233-the-round-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=native-americans">native-americans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=fiction-20th-century">fiction-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657693896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12090093790812817285">The Round House won the National Book Award for Fiction in 2012, and it has been on my tbr list almost that long, primarily thanks to a great review by Will Byrnes. So I finally read it and liked it a lot. It’s a coming-of-age story set on an Ojibwe reservation in North Dakota. It’s the story of Joe, a 13-year-old son, his father and judge Bazil and his mother Geraldine who returns home one day beaten and raped. <br/><br/>Joe’s decision to help solve the crime for his beloved mother is inspiring, as is hi</span>
  <span id="freeText12090093790812817285" style="display:none">The Round House won the National Book Award for Fiction in 2012, and it has been on my tbr list almost that long, primarily thanks to a great review by Will Byrnes. So I finally read it and liked it a lot. It’s a coming-of-age story set on an Ojibwe reservation in North Dakota. It’s the story of Joe, a 13-year-old son, his father and judge Bazil and his mother Geraldine who returns home one day beaten and raped. <br /><br />Joe’s decision to help solve the crime for his beloved mother is inspiring, as is his parents, and several secondary characters such as Mooshum, the elder who tells stories of Ojibwe history and spirituality, Grandma Ignatia who tells bawdy tales of her past, and Linda Wishkob, the twin who donates a kidney to her undeserving brother. <br /><br />One layer of this story is the long and continuing history, much fo it legal, that stole and continues to steal rights from Native Ameircans in this country, which finally weaves its way into this tale.<br /><br />“This book is set in 1988, but the tangle of laws that hinder prosecution of rape cases on many reservations still exists.”<br /><br />“1 in 3 Native women will be raped in her lifetime (and that figure is certainly higher as Native women often do not report rape); 86 percent of rapes and sexual assaults upon Native women are perpetrated by non-Native men; few are prosecuted.”<br /><br />"We want the right to prosecute criminals of all races on all lands within our original borders." <br /><br />I like Joe, who feels real and not idealized, not a saint. I also liked the connections to Ojibwe folklore, and all the representation of storytelling in this book. I was surprised in some ways by the resolution, but it's in many ways satisfying.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12090093790812817285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0j9EefeMDHSxiUgS/TtD7hVR6h7vIixbFWMOMKjakuGvBoMIuW8H8agpCZrHssxBxhsx9W1r0YeWmt/frvLyzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('si9VsCayHS8gDxiJaN+H/Op3LbIi8k/M/36dn5x80bDPFpLBaFEWqjmvWQFSVghTOT32WaC7shB8h0xwmlSxnA==')})
  }

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13438524-flight-behavior"><img alt="Flight Behavior" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1352212134l/13438524._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_13438524'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13438524-flight-behavior?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Flight Behavior<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/3541.Barbara_Kingsolver?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Barbara Kingsolver<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.78 avg rating &mdash; 84,076 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2012\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer12823675709119418313\">Flight Behavior takes on one of the most contentious subjects of our time: climate change. With a deft and versatile empathy Kingsolver dissects the motives that drive denial and belief in a precarious world.\n\nFlight Behavior transfixes from its open<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12823675709119418313\" style=\"display:none\">Flight Behavior takes on one of the most contentious subjects of our time: climate change. With a deft and versatile empathy Kingsolver dissects the motives that drive denial and belief in a precarious world.\n\nFlight Behavior transfixes from its opening scene, when a young woman\'s narrow experience of life is thrown wide with the force of a raging fire. In the lyrical language of her native Appalachia, Barbara Kingsolver bares the rich, tarnished humanity of her novel\'s inhabitants and unearths the modern complexities of rural existence. Characters and reader alike are quickly carried beyond familiar territory here, into the unsettled ground of science, faith, and everyday truces between reason and conviction. \n\nDellarobia Turnbow is a restless farm wife who gave up her own plans when she accidentally became pregnant at seventeen. Now, after a decade of domestic disharmony on a failing farm, she has settled for permanent disappointment but seeks momentary escape through an obsessive flirtation with a younger man. As she hikes up a mountain road behind her house to a secret tryst, she encounters a shocking sight: a silent, forested valley filled with what looks like a lake of fire. She can only understand it as a cautionary miracle, but it sparks a raft of other explanations from scientists, religious leaders, and the media. The bewildering emergency draws rural farmers into unexpected acquaintance with urbane journalists, opportunists, sightseers, and a striking biologist with his own stake in the outcome. As the community lines up to judge the woman and her miracle, Dellarobia confronts her family, her church, her town, and a larger world, in a flight toward truth that could undo all she has ever believed. \n\nFlight Behavior takes on one of the most contentious subjects of our time: climate change. With a deft and versatile empathy Kingsolver dissects the motives that drive denial and belief in a precarious world.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12823675709119418313\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9388.Louise_Erdrich">About Louise Erdrich</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9388.Louise_Erdrich"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1462224430p3/9388.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/9388.Louise_Erdrich">Louise Erdrich
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14302395727331005532">Karen Louise Erdrich is a American author of novels, poetry, and children's books. Her father is German American and mother is half Ojibwe and half French American. She is an enrolled member of the Anishinaabe nation (also known as Chippewa). She is widely acclaimed as one of the most significant Native writers of the second wave of what critic Kenneth Lincoln has called the Native American Renais</span>
  <span id="freeText14302395727331005532" style="display:none">Karen Louise Erdrich is a American author of novels, poetry, and children's books. Her father is German American and mother is half Ojibwe and half French American. She is an enrolled member of the Anishinaabe nation (also known as Chippewa). She is widely acclaimed as one of the most significant Native writers of the second wave of what critic Kenneth Lincoln has called the Native American Renaissance.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.answers.com/topic/louise-erdrich">http://www.answers.com/topic/louise-e...</a><br /><br />From a book description:<br /><p>Author Biography: </p><p>Louise Erdrich is one of the most gifted, prolific, and challenging of contemporary Native American novelists. Born in 1954 in Little Falls, Minnesota, she grew up mostly in Wahpeton, North Dakota, where her parents taught at Bureau of Indian Affairs schools. Her fiction reflects aspects of her mixed heritage: German through her father, and French and Ojibwa through her mother. She worked at various jobs, such as hoeing sugar beets, farm work, waitressing, short order cooking, lifeguarding, and construction work, before becoming a writer. She attended the Johns Hopkins creative writing program and received fellowships at the McDowell Colony and the Yaddo Colony. After she was named writer-in-residence at Dartmouth, she married professor Michael Dorris and raised several children, some of them adopted. She and Michael became a picture-book husband-and-wife writing team, though they wrote only one truly collaborative novel, <i>The Crown of Columbus</i> (1991).</p><p><i>The Antelope Wife</i> was published in 1998, not long after her separation from Michael and his subsequent suicide. Some reviewers believed they saw in <i>The Antelope Wife</i> the anguish Erdrich must have felt as her marriage crumbled, but she has stated that she is unconscious of having mirrored any real-life events.</p><p>She is the author of four previous bestselling andaward-winning novels, including <i>Love Medicine; The Beet Queen; Tracks; and The Bingo Palace. </i>She also has written two collections of poetry, <i>Jacklight, and Baptism of Desire.</i> Her fiction has been honored by the National Book Critics Circle (1984) and <i>The Los Angeles Times</i> (1985), and has been translated into fourteen languages. </p><p>Several of her short stories have been selected for O. Henry awards and for inclusion in the annual <i>Best American Short Story</i> anthologies. <i>The Blue Jay's Dance,</i> a memoir of motherhood, was her first nonfiction work, and her children's book, <i>Grandmother's Pigeon,</i> has been published by Hyperion Press. She lives in Minnesota with her children, who help her run a small independent bookstore called The Birchbark.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="14302395727331005532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
